# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with comprehensive findings about Kafka's SASL broker-side authentication implementation. The document includes:

### **40 Relevant Java Files** covering:

1. **Core Server Authenticator**: SaslServerAuthenticator - the main entry point for broker-side authentication
2. **Channel & Configuration**: ChannelBuilders, SaslChannelBuilder, JaasContext - mechanism selection and setup
3. **PLAIN SASL**: PlainSaslServer, PlainServerCallbackHandler, PlainLoginModule
4. **SCRAM SASL**: ScramSaslServer, ScramMechanism (SHA-256 & SHA-512), ScramServerCallbackHandler

7. **Callback Handlers**: AuthenticateCallbackHandler infrastructure and credential caches
8. **Protocol Messages**: SaslHandshakeRequest/Response, SaslAuthenticateRequest/Response
9. **JAAS Integration**: JaasContext, LoginManager, login implementations
10. **OAuth Bearer**: OAuthBearerSaslServer as additional mechanism
11. **Credential Management**: CredentialCache, DelegationTokenCache, CredentialProvider

### **Authentication Flow Chain**:
ChannelBuilders → SaslChannelBuilder → SaslServerAuthenticator → Mechanism-specific SaslServer (PLAIN/SCRAM/GSSAPI) → SaslAuthenticationContext

SaslAuthenticationContext\\n\\n## Mechanism Selection & Configuration\\n\\nThe **SaslChannelBuilder** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/SaslChannelBuilder.java) is responsible for:\\n- Maintaining Maps of enabled SASL mechanisms per listener\\n- Loading JAAS contexts using JaasContext.loadServerContext() for each enabled mechanism (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/JaasContext.java)\\n- Mapping mechanism-specific callback handlers\\n- Creating the appropriate callback handler instances based on mechanism type\\n- Managing credential caches for different SASL mechanisms\\n\\nConfiguration is driven by:\\n- **SaslConfigs** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/SaslConfigs.java) - defines SASL_MECHANISM, SASL_JAAS_CONFIG, SASL_CLIENT_CALLBACK_HANDLER_CLASS\\n- **BrokerSecurityConfigs** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/internals/BrokerSecurityConfigs.java) - defines SASL_ENABLED_MECHANISMS_CONFIG, SASL_SERVER_CALLBACK_HANDLER_CLASS_CONFIG, CONNECTIONS_MAX_REAUTH_MS_CONFIG\\n\\n## PLAIN SASL Mechanism Implementation\\n\\nThe PLAIN mechanism is implemented through:\\n- **PlainSaslServer** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainSaslServer.java) - implements SaslServer interface\\n- **PlainSaslServerProvider** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainSaslServerProvider.java) - provides factory for PlainSaslServer\\n- **PlainServerCallbackHandler** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainServerCallbackHandler.java) - implements AuthenticateCallbackHandler\\n- **PlainLoginModule** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/PlainLoginModule.java) - JAAS login module\\n\\n## SCRAM SASL Mechanism Implementation\\n\\nThe SCRAM mechanisms (SCRAM-SHA-256, SCRAM-SHA-512) are implemented through:\\n- **ScramSaslServer** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServer.java) - implements SaslServer interface, handles SCRAM protocol exchange\\n- **ScramSaslServerProvider** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServerProvider.java) - factory for both SCRAM-SHA-256 and SCRAM-SHA-512\\n- **ScramServerCallbackHandler** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramServerCallbackHandler.java) - implements AuthenticateCallbackHandler\\n- **ScramMechanism** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramMechanism.java) - enum defining SCRAM_SHA_256 and SCRAM_SHA_512\\n- **ScramFormatter** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramFormatter.java) - handles SCRAM credential generation\\n- **ScramMessages** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramMessages.java) - SCRAM protocol message handling\\n- **ScramCredentialUtils** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramCredentialUtils.java) - utilities for credential cache creation\\n- **ScramLoginModule** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/ScramLoginModule.java) - JAAS login module\\n- **ScramCredential** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/ScramCredential.java) - credential data class\\n\\n## GSSAPI/Kerberos SASL Mechanism Implementation\\n\\nGSSAPI (Kerberos) is handled by:\\n- **SaslServerAuthenticator.createSaslKerberosServer()** - creates Kerberos SaslServer\\n- **DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder.java) - extracts principal from Kerberos authentication\\n- Kerberos-specific JAAS context loading in SaslChannelBuilder\\n\\n## Authentication Context Lifecycle\\n\\nThe **SaslAuthenticationContext** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/auth/SaslAuthenticationContext.java) manages:\\n- Stores the SaslServer instance\\n- Maintains SecurityProtocol and client address information\\n- Implements the **AuthenticationContext** interface (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/auth/AuthenticationContext.java)\\n- Tracks listener name and optional TLS session information\\n- Lifecycle: created during handshake, used for principal extraction, closed after authentication\\n\\n## Callback Handler Infrastructure\\n\\n**AuthenticateCallbackHandler** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/auth/AuthenticateCallbackHandler.java) is the base interface that all server callback handlers implement. **SaslServerCallbackHandler** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/SaslServerCallbackHandler.java) provides default handling for:\\n- RealmCallback\\n- AuthorizeCallback (for GSSAPI)\\n- Custom mechanism-specific callbacks\\n\\n## Credential Management\\n\\n**CredentialCache** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/CredentialCache.java) manages credentials per mechanism:\\n- SCRAM credentials stored and retrieved by username\\n- **ScramCredentialCallback** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/ScramCredentialCallback.java) allows callback handlers to access credentials\\n- **DelegationTokenCache** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/token/delegation/internals/DelegationTokenCache.java) manages delegation token credentials\\n- **CredentialProvider** (server/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/security/CredentialProvider.java) coordinates cache management\\n\\n## SASL Protocol Messages\\n\\nThe SASL handshake and authentication use Kafka protocol messages:\\n- **SaslHandshakeRequest/Response** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/requests/SaslHandshakeRequest.java, Response.java) - mechanism negotiation\\n- **SaslAuthenticateRequest/Response** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/requests/SaslAuthenticateRequest.java, Response.java) - mechanism-specific tokens\\n- **SaslExtensions/SaslExtensionsCallback** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/auth/SaslExtensions*.java) - mechanism extensions\\n\\n## JAAS Integration\\n\\n**JaasContext** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/JaasContext.java) provides:\\n- loadServerContext() - loads server JAAS configuration for specific listener and mechanism\\n- Configuration entry management from JAAS config files or dynamic configuration\\n- **LoginManager** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/LoginManager.java) - manages login lifecycle per mechanism\\n- **AbstractLogin/DefaultLogin** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/AbstractLogin.java, DefaultLogin.java) - login implementations\\n\\n## Additional SASL Mechanism (OAuth Bearer)\\n\\n**OAuthBearerSaslServer** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/oauthbearer/internals/OAuthBearerSaslServer.java) and **OAuthBearerValidatorCallbackHandler** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/oauthbearer/OAuthBearerValidatorCallbackHandler.java) implement OAuth Bearer token authentication.\\n\\n## Error Handling\\n\\n**SaslAuthenticationException** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/errors/SaslAuthenticationException.java) is thrown for SASL-specific authentication failures.\\n\\n## Configuration & Internal Details\\n\\n**SaslInternalConfigs** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/SaslInternalConfigs.java) defines internal SASL configuration like credential lifetime management for session-based reauthentication.\\n\\nThe complete authentication flow: Client connects \u2192 ChannelBuilders creates SaslChannelBuilder \u2192 SaslChannelBuilder creates SaslServerAuthenticator \u2192 SaslServerAuthenticator performs handshake \u2192 mechanism selected \u2192 appropriate SaslServer created (PLAIN/SCRAM/GSSAPI) \u2192 SaslAuthenticationContext established \u2192 credentials validated via callbacks \u2192 authentication complete.\"\n}\n",
